## Scientists explore the anatomy of a ‘zombie volcano’ that’s showing signs of activity

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/science/uturuncu-zombie-volcano-erupt)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 14:10:00-20:10_

### Summary

Scientists have explored the anatomy of a 'zombie volcano' named Uturuncu, a 250,000-year-old mountain in the Central Andes range, which is showing signs of activity. The research, published in the Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences, combined satellite data, seismic activity, and computer models to uncover the cause of the volcano's unrest. It revealed that magma, gases, and briny fluids were interacting within a hydrothermal network, not surging magma, leading to quakes, steam release, and volcano deformation. The study found that as the magma body heated subterranean liquid and released gases, the gas and liquid migrated upward and collected in chambers below the volcanic crater. The findings suggest that Uturuncu's activity is not a sign of an imminent eruption, but rather a 'zombie' volcano degassing, letting off steam. The research has implications for understanding volcanoes, identifying potential targets for geothermal energy, and accessing minerals essential for technology. The study was conducted using multiple techniques, including seismic activity, rock chemistry, and physics analysis, to create a clearer picture of the volcano's internal structure.

### Key Takeaways
  - Scientists have explored the anatomy of a 'zombie volcano,' which is Uturuncu, a mountain in the Central Andes range, showing signs of activity without erupting for over 250,000 years.

### Named Entities
- **Uturuncu**
    - A  lofty peak in the Central Andes mountain range, a ‘zombie volcano’ with signs of activity.
    - Uturuncu is the main subject of the study, highlighting the ongoing research about a dormant volcano showing signs of activity.
- **Mindy Weisberger**
    - The author of the article.
    - She is the primary source of information for this news article.
- **Magma Body**
    - A vast reservoir of magma lying beneath Uturuncu, a part of the Altiplano-Puna Magma Body.
    - It's a key element in understanding the activity at Uturuncu and the interaction between magma and fluids.
- **Zombie Volcano**
    - Uturuncu, and other similar dormant volcanoes.
    - It's a key term used to describe Uturuncu, which is the central subject of the study and the focal point of this article.
- **Seismic Events**
    - More than 1,700 seismic events between 2009 and 2012.
    - They were used to produce high-resolution images of the shallow crust under Uturuncu and to reveal details about the volcano's inner workings.
- **Hydrothermal Network**
    - A system of interacting magma, gases, and briny fluids.
    - It's the key system discovered to be causing the volcano's unrest and activity.
- **Magma Chamber**
    - A subsurface pocket of magma that could potentially erupt through vents and fissures.
    - It's the primary source of volcanic activity, and the study found that Uturuncu's activity is linked to this chamber.
- **Altiplano-Puna Magma Body**
    - A vast reservoir of magma spanning roughly 124 miles (200 kilometers) beneath Uturuncu.
    - It's described as the biggest known active magma body in the planet's crust, and its interaction with the hydrothermal network is key to understanding Uturuncu's activity.
- **Geothermal Energy**
    - Potential energy source that zombie volcanoes like Uturuncu could be explored as.
    - The study suggests that investigating Uturuncu could lead to the exploration of geothermal energy sources in other zombie volcanoes.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-04-28**
    - The date of the study published in the journal Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences.
  - **2025-05-05**
    - The date when the article was updated and CNN republished the news.
  - **2025-04-26**
    - The date when the satellite radar imagery was taken of Uturuncu, the tallest mountain in southwestern Bolivia.

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _2025-04-26_ to _2025-04-28_**
    - The time frame when the study was conducted and analyzed, leading to the findings published in the journal Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences.
  - **From _2025-04-26_ to _2025-05-05_**
    - The time frame when the CNN article was updated and republished, keeping the information current.
  - **From _2025-04-26_ to _2025-04-28_**
    - The time frame when the satellite imagery was taken and the subsequent research began, focusing on understanding Uturuncu's activity.

## Skechers is going private during the middle of a trade war

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/business/skechers-shoes-3g-capital)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 15:59:00-04:00_

### Summary

Skechers, a shoe company based in Southern California with 5,300 US stores, is planning to go private by being purchased by investment firm 3G Capital for $9.4 billion. CEO Robert Greenberg of Skechers stated in a statement that the company is entering 'its next chapter in partnership with the global investment firm 3G Capital.' The move to go private comes amid a trade war during which President Trump's tariffs have heavily impacted the footwear industry. Skechers' stock jumped 25% on the news of the acquisition. The company is getting off the public market due to the influence of tariffs, which have made it more attractive to be taken private. Other struggling companies may consider similar moves in the future as a response to volatility. Sneakers, which are 99% manufactured overseas, are highly exposed to tariffs, and Skechers, being an American shoe company, has seen its share prices fall due to fears of the impact of tariffs on its operations. Skechers previously withdrew its financial guidance due to the uncertainty around tariffs, and other companies in the footwear industry have urged the president to exempt the footwear industry from tariffs.

### Key Takeaways

Portnoy, who is Jewish, expressed fury about the sign and fired two servers who were involved. Temple University is investigating the incident and suspended the student involved. ## A Woman Missing for Over 60 Years Found Alive, Police Say She Made Own Choice to Disappear

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/us/audrey-backeberg-missing-found-alive)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 13:18:00-20:18_

### Summary

An 82-year-old woman, Audrey Jean Backeberg, who vanished from Reedsburg, Wisconsin on July 7, 1962, has been found. According to the Sauk County Sheriff's Office, Backeberg made the decision to disappear on her own, and her disappearance was not the result of any criminal activity or foul play. The investigation, which was reopened due to a new look at cold case files by Detective Isaac Hanson, was aided by a genealogy site and a review of her sister's Ancestry.com account. The detective spent 45 minutes on the phone with Backeberg, who sounded happy with her decision to leave. The sheriff's office concluded that Backeberg’s disappearance was her own choice and not a result of any criminal behavior.

### Key Takeaways

  - Backeberg reportedly made the decision to disappear on her own.
  - Her disappearance was not a result of any criminal activity or foul play.
  - An investigation was reopened, leading to new evidence that eventually led to the finding.

## Marijuana is extremely dangerous to the fetus in the womb, study finds

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/health/marijuana-prenatal-harm-wellness)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 12:49:00.000-04:00_

### Summary

A new meta-analysis of research has found that using marijuana during pregnancy is linked to poor fetal development, low infant birth weight, dangerously early deliveries, and even death. The analysis, led by Dr. Jamie Lo, an obstetrician at Oregon Health & Science University, and published in JAMA Pediatrics, analyzed 51 studies with over 21 million participants. The findings indicate that use of marijuana during pregnancy is associated with a 52% higher risk of preterm delivery before 37 weeks and a 75% higher risk of low birth weight. The study also found a 29% higher risk of infant death associated with the use of marijuana during pregnancy. Despite the potential harms, marijuana use during pregnancy is rising, and there is a misconception that it is harmless due to its natural origins. The new research suggests that as more studies are conducted with consistent results, there is more certainty that there is an association between prenatal exposure to cannabis and adverse birth outcomes. Experts also highlight the risks of cognitive decline and dementia, complications during surgery, cancers, and mental disorders in children of marijuana users.

### Key Takeaways
  - Marijuana use during pregnancy is linked to poor fetal development, low infant birth weight, dangerously early deliveries and even death, according to a new meta-analysis of research.

### Named Entities
- **Jamie Lo**
    - Lead study author and obstetrician who conducted the new meta-analysis on the impact of marijuana use during pregnancy.
    - Jamie Lo's role as the study lead and author is crucial as she provides the expert insights and data from the study.
- **JAMA Pediatrics**
    - The peer-reviewed medical journal where the new meta-analysis was published.
    - As the journal where the study was published, it provides credibility and the reach of the findings.
- **Oregon Health & Science University**
    - The university where Dr. Jamie Lo is an associate professor.
    - The university affiliation adds to the credibility of the study and its author.
- **National Institute on Drug Abuse**
    - A government agency that conducted the 2019 analysis of over 450,000 pregnant American women ages 12 to 44 regarding cannabis use.
    - The agency's analysis of cannabis use during pregnancy helps contextualize the findings of the new meta-analysis.
- **US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention**
    - The US government agency that provides health information on the health risks of smoking.
    - The CDC's information on the health risks of smoking complements the discussion about the dangers of marijuana use during pregnancy.
- **Colorado School of Public Health Anschutz Medical Campus**
    - The medical campus where Brianna Moore, the assistant professor who commented on the new study, teaches.
    - Moore's expertise and perspective on the study add to the credibility of the article.
- **Brianna Moore**
    - The assistant professor of epidemiology at the Colorado School of Public Health who commented on the new study.
    - Moore's perspective provides additional insights and context to the article's discussion.
- **CNN**
    - The news source that published the article on the study findings.
    - As the news source, CNN disseminates the article widely to the public.

### Important Dates
  - **2022-05-05**
    - The date of publication of the CNN article on marijuana use during pregnancy.
  - **2022-05-05**
    - The publication date for the new meta-analysis in JAMA Pediatrics.

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _2025-05-05_ to _2025-05-05_**
    - The date of the CNN article on marijuana use during pregnancy, highlighting the recent development in the knowledge about the potential harms of marijuana use during pregnancy.
  - **From _2025-05-05_ to _2025-05-05_**
    - The publication date for the new meta-analysis in JAMA Pediatrics, indicating the emerging consensus on the risks associated with marijuana use during pregnancy.

## What to do if your flight is canceled or delayed in the US and UK?

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/travel/flight-canceled-delayed-what-to-do)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 12:28:00-04:00_

### Summary

A CNN article outlines advice for travelers dealing with flight delays and cancellations at Newark Liberty International Airport in New Jersey, where air traffic controller staffing shortages are causing major disruptions. The article provides tips to travelers on what to do before arriving at the airport, if they find themselves at the airport unexpectedly, and what to do if their flight is canceled or delayed. It covers topics such as checking flight status, approaching airline agents with a positive attitude, using frequent flyer miles, and seeking accommodation if stranded overnight. Additionally, it mentions that United Airlines has reduced its daily roundtrip flights to minimize disruptions, and the article explains that cooperation between airlines and the use of frequent flyer miles can help. The article also advises travelers to consider buying travel insurance for additional coverage and to keep receipts for any airport purchases. Furthermore, it notes that since October 28, 2024, airlines in the United States are required to give passengers cash refunds for significant flight delays or cancellations, not vouchers.

### Key Takeaways
  - Travelers should check their flight status before they go to the airport to avoid the inconvenience of a long drive.
  - Airlines' agents can offer the most help in resolving delays or cancellations, and a positive attitude can make a difference.
  - Consider using frequent flyer miles if the demand for flights is high during a weather event.
  - Trapped for the night? Airlines may not be legally required to provide accommodation, but they can offer it, and you may be able to claim the cost back later.
  - Travelers should consider buying travel insurance to cover additional risks of flight delays or cancellations.
  - Airlines are now required to give cash refunds for significant flight delays or cancellations in the US, not vouchers.

### Named Entities
- **Scott Keyes**
    - Founder of Going.com, a travel information website.
    - Scott Keyes offers tips on what to do if a flight is delayed or canceled, providing practical advice for travelers.
- **Lousson Smith**
    - Product operations specialist at Going.com.
    - Lousson Smith offers insights into cooperation between airlines and the availability of flights with frequent flyer miles during cancellations.
- **Julian Kheel**
    - Founder and CEO of Points Path, a travel planning company.
    - Julian Kheel discusses how frequent flyer programs can be used during flight cancellations to avoid high costs.
- **Forrest Brown**
    - CNN reporter who published the article.
    - Forrest Brown provides the initial news piece, outlining the issue of flight delays and cancellations at Newark Liberty International Airport and the general advice on what to do in such situations.
- **New Jersey**
    - The state where Newark Liberty International Airport is located.
    - New Jersey's Newark Liberty International Airport is mentioned as the hub where air traffic controller staffing shortages have caused major disruptions.
- **United Airlines**
    - One of the airlines mentioned in the article.
    - United Airlines has reduced its daily roundtrip flights to minimize disruptions at Newark Liberty International Airport.
- **Newark Liberty International Airport**
    - The specific airport where delays and cancellations are occurring.
    - The article focuses on the specific airport experiencing disruptions, providing context for the flight status advice and tips.
- **Scott Keyes**
    - Founder of Going.com, a travel information website.
    - Scott Keyes is mentioned again for his tips on handling flight delays and cancellations.
- **United States**
    - The country where the advice applies.
    - The article provides advice that can be applied to travelers in the United States, regardless of which airline they are using.
- **UK Civil Aviation Authority (CAA)**
    - A regulatory body in the UK.
    - The CAA advises on what to do if a flight is canceled or delayed in the UK, and the traveler is in the UK.

The jurors will be instructed to avoid media coverage during the trial to ensure a fair and impartial decision. The article also mentions the potential biases jurors may have based on public opinion and the numerous civil suits against Combs, which may affect their judgment during the trial. The article is written by Sandra Gonzalez and is sourced from CNN.

## People close to the fan who fell onto field at PNC Park share positive update

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/03/sport/pnc-park-fan-fall-update-spt)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 11:13:00-20:13_

### Summary

The fan who fell onto the field at PNC Park during a Chicago Cubs and Pittsburgh Pirates game on Wednesday has made a positive recovery, according to updates from his girlfriend and family. The 20-year-old, identified as Kavan Markwood, was in critical condition after falling from the right field wall, but now, Jennifer Phillips, his mother, has reported that he is awake, alert, and able to speak. The incident is being treated as accidental. Markwood, who graduated from South Allegheny High School in 2022 and played football for both Walsh University and Wheeling University, was recognized for his resilience, strength, and kindness. The family has started a GoFundMe campaign to support Markwood's recovery. His high school and college alma mater have also shared their condolences and support. The incident has also sparked a fundraising effort on Kavan’s behalf, with more than $27,000 raised as of Saturday evening.

### Key Takeaways
  - A fan, identified as Kavan Markwood, fell onto the field at PNC Park during a game, but was later described as 'awake and continuing to work toward making his body stronger each day.'

- _Published: 2025-05-05 10:20:00-20:20_

### Summary

Britain is marking the 80th anniversary of VE Day, the day Nazi Germany surrendered to Allied forces, with four days of commemorations. London's commemorations began on Monday with a military parade that featured members of the United Kingdom's armed forces. The parade was watched by members of the royal family including King Charles and Queen Camilla, who wore uniforms reflecting personal military ties and historical resonance. Events will continue across the UK, including the installation of 30,000 ceramic poppies at the Tower of London to remember those killed in conflict. The King and Queen led the royal family onto the Buckingham Palace balcony to cheers from the crowd. The commemorative mood comes amid renewed tensions within the royal family, as Prince Harry revealed that he cannot imagine bringing his family back to the UK after a court case over his security arrangements.

## Scottie Scheffler ties PGA Tour record to claim first victory of 2025 at the CJ Cup Byron Nelson

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/sport/scottie-sheffler-cj-cup-byron-nelson-record-pga-tour-spt-intl)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 10:18:00-05:00_

### Summary

Scottie Scheffler achieved a historic victory at the CJ Cup Byron Nelson, tying the PGA Tour record by shooting 253 in the 72-hole scoring. This feat, previously set by Justin Thomas in 2017 and Ludvig Åberg in 2023, marked Scheffler's first victory of the year. The 28-year-old player, who has won ten times in the past three years, celebrated with his newborn son, emphasizing the personal significance of this victory. Scheffler's success at TPC Craig Ranch, the venue of the tournament, showcased his skills and dedication to the sport, highlighting his impact on the PGA Tour.

### Key Takeaways
  - Scottie Scheffler tied the PGA Tour record by shooting 253 in the 72-hole scoring to win his first victory of 2025 at the CJ Cup Byron Nelson.
  - Scheffler became the first player to achieve this feat, equaling Justin Thomas' score from the 2017 Sony Open and Ludvig Åberg's from the 2023 RSM Classic.
  - Scheffler also broke the CJ Cup's 72-hole record, previously set by Steven Bowditch in 2015 with a score of 259.
  - His win was particularly special as it was the first of the year for Scheffler, who had already won 10 times in the past three years, including two Masters victories.
  - Scheffler celebrated his victory while holding his newborn son, marking a significant personal milestone and a reunion with family memories from his childhood.
  - The victory was a result of Scheffler putting in a dominant performance, which included a final-round 63 to finish at 31-under-par.
  - He expressed gratitude for his family, acknowledging the sacrifices and support of those around him that helped him achieve this milestone.

The International Court of Justice has dismissed Sudan's case against the UAE, alleging the UAE supported paramilitary forces in Darfur region and violated the Genocide Convention. The ongoing civil war in Sudan since April 2023 has caused the world's worst humanitarian catastrophe, and diplomatic efforts to resolve the conflict have failed.

  - The ongoing civil war in Sudan, since April 2023, has caused the world’s worst humanitarian catastrophe, and diplomatic efforts to resolve the conflict have failed.

The article notes that this response is part of a larger context of the Trump administration's changes to science policy, including the cancellation of hundreds of research grants due to the inclusion of the word 'diversity' in some programs.

## Four-time grand slam champion Naomi Osaka wins first title since becoming a mother

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/sport/naomi-osaka-wins-first-title-maternity-spt-intl)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 09:15:00-20:15_

### Summary

Four-time grand slam champion Naomi Osaka has triumphed in her first title since becoming a mother, defeating Kaja Juvan 6-1, 7-5 in the final of L’Open 35 de Saint-Malo, a WTA 125 event in France. The win marks Osaka's first clay-court victory and places her back within the top 50 rankings for the first time since her return to competitive tennis after giving birth to her daughter in July 2023. Osaka described her win as 'ironic' given her perception of the surface as her 'worst,' reflecting the challenges she faced returning to tennis after the birth of her daughter. The article notes that Osaka has previously taken extended breaks from tennis to prioritize her mental health, and this latest title comes after a promising start to the year was interrupted by injuries.

### Key Takeaways
  - Four-time grand slam champion Naomi Osaka won her first title since becoming a mother at the L’Open 35 de Saint-Malo tennis tournament.
  - Osaka defeated Slovenian player Kaja Juvan to win the title, marking her first clay-court victory.
  - Osaka is now ranked within the top 50 for the first time since her return to tennis after giving birth.
  - She described her win as 'ironic' as she thought this surface was her 'worst' and shared her gratitude for her support system during her recovery and journey back to tennis.

### Named Entities
- **Matias Grez**
    - CNN reporter who wrote the article.

## Some US cities are canceling cultural events over fears of ICE raids and deportations

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/03/us/cultural-events-canceled-trump-deportations)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 08:06:00.000Z_

### Summary

Some US cities have canceled cultural events over fears of ICE raids and deportations, especially during the Trump administration. Chicago's Cinco de Mayo parade and festival, Philadelphia’s El Carnaval de Puebla, and central Oregon’s Latino Fest were among the events canceled or downsized due to community concerns. UnidosUs, a major Hispanic civil rights organization, has found that 43% of Latino voters fear immigration authorities will arrest people, even if they are US citizens. The Trump administration's crackdown on undocumented immigrants and its efforts to target schools, churches, and deport immigrants for alleged gang ties have led to these cultural events cancellations. Organizations are prioritizing community safety over celebrating cultural events, highlighting the impact of the Trump administration's immigration policies on public events and cultural practices.

## Immunotherapy helps certain cancer patients avoid surgery: 'We hope this is the future'

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/health/immunotherapy-cancer-patients-study-wellness)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 07:30:00-20:30_

### Summary

The article discusses how immunotherapy, specifically the drug dostarlimab, has the potential to treat certain cancer patients without surgery or other invasive treatments. Kelly Spill, a 28-year-old diagnosed with stage III rectal cancer, was one of 117 participants in a study published in the New England Journal of Medicine. The study found that patients with mismatch repair-deficient or dMMR cancer, including rectal cancer, could be cured with the drug without the need for surgery, radiation, or chemotherapy. The findings could have significant implications for treating various solid tumors. However, the study noted that the treatment may not work for everyone, and patients with the specific genetic mutations must be identified and tested prior to treatment. The article highlights the potential for a new age of cancer care, where treatments can be less invasive and more tailored to individual patients. Additionally, it mentions that colorectal cancer cases among young adults are on the rise, underscoring the need for improved treatment options for this population.

### Key Takeaways
  - Kelly Spill, a 28-year-old diagnosed with stage III rectal cancer, was able to avoid surgery and other invasive treatments due to a new immunotherapy drug called dostarlimab.
  - The study, published in the New England Journal of Medicine, found that immunotherapy can cure certain cancer types in patients without surgery or other invasive treatments.
  - The study involved 117 cancer patients with mismatch repair-deficient or dMMR cancer, of which 80% did not require surgery, radiation, or chemotherapy after six months of treatment.
  - The research has implications for treating a wide range of solid tumors, not just rectal cancer.
  - The findings suggest a new age of cancer care where immunotherapy treatments could be used to treat cancer in a non-invasive manner, preserving organs and allowing for normal life post-cancer treatment.

Prosecutors have led the case this time with new special prosecutor Hank Brennan, while the defense team has changed and includes Robert Alessi and Victoria George. The use of media interviews and videos of Read, including her statements that she may have hit the victim, have been presented as evidence. A major change is the firing of lead investigator Michael Proctor, who was fired for sending sexist and offensive messages, undermining the prosecution's case. Despite these changes, it remains unclear if Read will testify and whether Proctor will be a key witness in the retrial.

### Key Takeaways

## How one man just rewrote the history of Alcatraz

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/04/11/travel/alcatraz-3d-mapping-pete-kelsey-nps)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 07:07:00-05:00_

### Summary

A technologist named Pete Kelsey was tasked with mapping Alcatraz Island to preserve it for future generations. Using LiDAR technology and drones, Kelsey's team mapped the entire island, including areas previously inaccessible due to safety concerns. The project aimed to provide baseline data for future surveys on climate change, seismic activity, and deterioration of the site. The data can now be used for scientific predictions and also in the arts, such as for movie directors and virtual tourism purposes. The project took more than a year to complete, starting in December 2023, and involved overcoming several challenges, including restrictions from the National Park Service and waiting for nesting season to end for seabirds.

### Key Takeaways
  - A technologist, Pete Kelsey, was tasked with mapping Alcatraz Island to preserve it for future generations and to make its invisible structures visible.
  - The project involved the use of LiDAR technology to create 3D maps of the island, including Civil War-era spaces, and to monitor and predict future changes to the site.
  - The mapping process took more than a year due to restrictions from the National Park Service and the need to wait for nesting season to end for seabirds.
  - Kelsey and his team were able to gain access to areas previously off-limits due to safety concerns.
  - The mapping project will be used for scientific predictions about climate change and seismic activity, as well as for the arts, such as replicating the prison for movie directors and virtual tourism purposes.

### Named Entities
- **Pete Kelsey**
    - A technologist specializing in 3D data capture who was tasked with mapping Alcatraz.
    - Kelsey was the key figure who initiated and led the project of mapping Alcatraz, making it a crucial entity for the article.
- **Alcatraz**
    - The island site in San Francisco Bay where a 29-year federal penitentiary was located and later used for military purposes and Indigenous activism.
    - Alcatraz is the main subject of the article and Kelsey's mapping project is centered on this iconic site, making it a central entity.
- **LiDAR**
    - An airborne mapping technique which uses laser scanning to create three-dimensional models with centimeter accuracy.
    - LiDAR is a critical tool used in the project, playing a significant role in Kelsey's mapping efforts.
- **National Park Service**
    - The organization managing Alcatraz Island, which imposed restrictions on drone usage and access.
    - The National Park Service's restrictions were a challenge in the mapping project, as they were in charge of the island's management.
- **Civil War**
    - A military conflict where Alcatraz served as a fort to protect San Francisco.
    - The Civil War-era structures on the island are of historical interest and were mapped as part of the project.
- **Indigenous activists**
    - Groups who occupied Alcatraz in 1969 in the name of Native American civil rights.
    - Their occupation of Alcatraz is another historical event that the mapping project brings to light.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-05**
    - The date when the article was updated and the CNN source was last accessed.

### Important Timeframes

    - The timeframe when the project of mapping Alcatraz was initiated and completed.
  - **From _2025-05-05_ to _2025-05-05_**
    - The timeframe when the article was updated.

## Huge ‘Hobbit’-themed eagle sculptures to depart New Zealand airport

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/travel/eagle-sculptures-wellington-airport-hobbit-intl-scli)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 06:44:00.000Z_

### Summary

Two giant eagle sculptures, inspired by 'The Hobbit' and 'The Lord of the Rings' movies, have been standing at Wellington Airport for more than a decade, coinciding with the release of Peter Jackson's 'The Hobbit' movie trilogy. Made by Weta Workshop, the team behind the movie's props, the eagles weigh 1.2 tons and have a 15-meter wingspan. They are a popular attraction, drawing tourists to the airport. These eagles, which symbolize the characters' heroic and protective roles in Tolkien's stories, will depart on Friday, marking the end of their 12-year tenure at the airport. Wellington Airport’s chief executive, Matt Clarke, expressed the eagles' significance and noted the airport will work with Weta Workshop to create a unique, locally-themed replacement for them.

### Key Takeaways
  - Two giant eagle sculptures inspired by 'The Hobbit' and 'The Lord of the Rings' are being relocated from Wellington Airport on Friday.

    - She is the person who wrote about the relocation of the eagle sculptures from Wellington Airport.

    - He is the author whose work inspired the eagle sculptures, making the airport synonymous with his fictional universe.
- **Peter Jackson**
    - The director of the 'Hobbit' movie trilogy, whose films featured the giant eagle sculptures.
    - His films were the catalyst for the eagles being installed at the airport, as they were filmed in New Zealand.
- **Matt Clarke**
    - The chief executive of Wellington Airport.
    - He is the one who provided a statement about the eagles, indicating his perspective on their importance to the airport.
- **Weta Workshop**
    - The team that created the props and physical effects for 'The Hobbit' and 'The Lord of the Rings' trilogies, including the eagle sculptures.
    - They are responsible for creating the sculptures and likely have a role in deciding what to replace them with.
- **Smaug**
    - The antagonist dragon in 'The Hobbit' whose sculpture will remain at Wellington Airport.
    - As a significant character from the 'Hobbit' films, the Smaug sculpture will be retained, providing a connection to the airport's heritage.

## Indiana Pacers stun Cleveland Cavaliers in Game 1 despite Donovan Mitchell breaking Michael Jordan playoff record

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/sport/indiana-pacers-cleveland-cavaliers-game-1-spt-intl)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 06:23:00-20:23_

### Summary

The Indiana Pacers defeated the Cleveland Cavaliers 121-112 in Game 1 of the Eastern Conference semifinals, showcasing a team effort led by Tyrese Haliburton, who had 22 points, 13 assists, three rebounds, three blocks, and a steal. Despite Donovan Mitchell setting a record with 33 points in Game 1, Cleveland failed to secure the win. On the other hand, the Golden State Warriors won Game 7 against the Houston Rockets with Buddy Hield leading with a game-high 33 points on 12-of-15 shooting and an absurd 9-of-11 from three-point range. Steph Curry led the Warriors with 22 points, 10 rebounds, seven assists, two steals, and two blocks. The game was marked by poor shooting from distance for Cleveland, leading them to miss a lot of good looks and ultimately costing them the game.

### Key Takeaways
  - Indiana Pacers won Game 1 of the Eastern Conference semifinals against the Cleveland Cavaliers 121-112, despite Donovan Mitchell setting a record by scoring 33 points in the opening game of the series.
  - Tyrese Haliburton led the Pacers with 22 points, 13 assists, three rebounds, three blocks, and a steal.
  - Andrew Nembhard had a team-high 23 points for Indiana, including 5-of-6 from three-point range.
  - Cleveland was without Darius Garland for a third straight game, with Evan Mobley scoring 20 points and 10 rebounds and Ty Jerome adding 21 points off the bench.
  - The Cavaliers missed a lot of good looks, costing them in Game 1 where they went 9-of-38 from deep, including 1-of-11 from Mitchell.
  - The Warriors won Game 7 against the Houston Rockets, with Buddy Hield scoring a game-high 33 points on 12-of-15 shooting and an absurd 9-of-11 from three-point range in the fourth quarter.
  - Steph Curry contributed 22 points, 10 rebounds, seven assists, two steals, and two blocks, while Jimmy Butler had 20 points, eight rebounds, and seven assists.
  - Fred VanVleet scored 17 points for the Rockets in Game 7, on a shooting night with the team going 9-of-38 from deep and 1-of-11 from Mitchell.

### Named Entities
- **Indiana Pacers**
    - NBA team that won the game against Cleveland Cavaliers.
    - The winning team, Indiana Pacers, is the central entity of the article focusing on their victory against the Cleveland Cavaliers in Game 1 of the Eastern Conference semifinals.

## Temu says it’s only shipping from the US. That doesn’t mean the products are made here

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/03/business/temu-shipping-us-china-de-minimis-tariffs)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 06:01:00+00:00_

### Summary

Chinese e-commerce site Temu announced that all its American sales would now be handled by US-based sellers, fulfilling orders from within the US. This marks a significant shift, as the platform had previously used the de minimis exemption to flood the US market with low-cost goods. The de minimis loophole allowed shipments of goods worth $800 or less to enter the US duty-free, often bypassing time-consuming inspections and paperwork. With the Trump administration imposing tariffs on all Chinese imports, Temu's new model shows how major companies could evade these tariffs and adopt alternative strategies. The site will now fulfill orders from local warehouses, but the products may not be made in the USA, as they are often manufactured in China and imported directly to the US. Temu claims that its pricing for US consumers remains unchanged as the platform transitions to a local fulfillment model. However, some customers have reported that items are out of stock or subject to additional fees. The change is a response to the Trump administration's tariffs, the de minimis exemption being used by Chinese e-commerce sites to gain a competitive edge in the US market.

### Key Takeaways
  - Temu, a Chinese e-commerce site, has announced it will now fulfill all American orders from US-based sellers, marking a significant shift in its shipping model

### Named Entities
- **Temu**
    - A Chinese e-commerce site that will now fulfill all American orders from US-based sellers.
    - The main subject of the article, highlighting the changes to its business model.
- **Donald Trump**
    - The US President who imposed punishing tariffs on all Chinese imports.
    - The context in which Temu's actions are framed, showing a potential evasion of Trump's tariffs.
- **US President Donald Trump**
    - The US President who imposed tariffs on Chinese imports.
    - The context in which Temu's actions are framed, showing a potential evasion of the tariffs.

Bush's experience in 2008, highlighting ongoing public anger in Kenya. The incident occurred against the backdrop of Ruto's attempts to address public discontent by abandoning tax hikes and inviting opposition members into his cabinet, but the cost of living remains a significant source of public frustration in the country.

The tariff announcement comes as the movie industry in the U.S. is struggling due to a decrease in the number of major pictures hitting theaters and a shift towards streaming services. However, the implementation of such a tariff is unclear as films are intellectual property and not traditionally subject to tariffs. The USTR notes that some services, including film production, could be subject to certain non-tariff trade barriers, which could potentially disadvantage American filmmaking.

## What We Know About the Massive Staffing Shortage Causing 7 Days of Major Delays at Newark Airport

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/04/us/newark-airport-nj-united-flights-delays)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 03:48:00-04:00_

### Summary

For years, the shortage of certified air traffic controllers in the U.S. has led to flight disruptions and headaches for travelers across the country. This issue has been particularly problematic at busy Newark Liberty International Airport in New Jersey, where staffing issues have led to major delays for an unprecedented seventh day in a row. The Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) on Sunday implemented a Ground Delay Program and flights were delayed an average of almost four hours Sunday evening. The reasons for these delays include a nationwide air traffic controller shortage, a walk-off by Newark air traffic controllers, the closure of a runway for rehabilitation work, and technology failures caused by outdated equipment. Newark Airport's control facility responsible for traffic has been 'chronically understaffed for years,' and the shortage is at its lowest point in nearly 30 years. The FAA is using delays to slow the number of flights so the system remains safe, and the President is calling for Congress to provide the resources needed to upgrade the technology. The controllers union, flight attendants, and airlines are calling for more air traffic controllers and better technology to mitigate the delays and ensure safety for travelers.

### Key Takeaways
  - Newark Liberty International Airport has experienced unprecedented seven days of major delays, with flights delayed an average of almost four hours on Sunday evening, according to the FAA advisory.

## Children aged 14 or younger now make up less than 12% of this country’s population

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/asia/japan-child-population-fall-intl-hnk)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 12:20:00-13:20_

### Summary

Japan's estimated child population has decreased for the 44th straight year, standing at a record low of 13.66 million children aged 14 and under as of April 1, 2025, representing just 11.1% of the total population of 123.4 million. This demographic crisis is attributed to a falling birth rate and a rapidly aging population. The fertility rate remains at 1.3, significantly below the 2.1 required to maintain a stable population. The government has launched initiatives such as expanding child care facilities and offering housing subsidies to boost fertility rates and incentivize marriage. However, Japan is described as a 'super-aged' nation with more than 20% of the population over the age of 65, and the total population is expected to drop to about 88 million by 2065. The article notes that several other East Asian and European countries, including China, South Korea, and Italy, have also experienced population decline, but Japan's unique approach focuses on fertility rates and family incentives, rather than embracing immigration as a solution.

### Key Takeaways
  - Japan's child population has decreased for the 44th consecutive year, standing at a record low of 13.66 million children aged 14 or younger as of April 1, 2025, representing 11.1% of the total population of 123.4 million.
  - Japan's fertility rate has been relatively flat at 1.3 in recent years, falling short of the 2.1 required to maintain a stable population.
  - The falling birth rate and aging population have become a significant concern for Japan, leading to a workforce decline, economic challenges, and changes in social structures.
  - Japan is described as a 'super-aged' nation with more than 20% of the population over the age of 65, with projections indicating that the population may drop to about 88 million in 2065.
  - Demographic factors influencing the decrease in Japan's child population include high living costs, a weak yen, economic stagnation, high inflation, a demanding work culture, and limited housing availability.
  - Government efforts to address the issue have included launching initiatives such as expanding child care facilities, offering housing subsidies to parents, and paying couples to have children.
  - Several other East Asian and European countries, including China, South Korea, and Italy, have also experienced population decline, but Japan's approach to the issue is somewhat unique in its focus on fertility rates and family incentives, compared to other countries that have embraced immigration as a solution.

### Named Entities
- **Kathleen Magramo and Junko Ogura**
    - Authors of the news article
    - The news article was written and published by these authors, providing a source of the information.
- **Children’s Day**
    - A public holiday celebrated in Japan
    - The article discusses the demographics leading up to this holiday, highlighting the trend of fewer children in Japan's population.
- **Japan**
    - The country of focus in this article
    - The demographic crisis and child population decline are presented as specific issues affecting Japan's population.
- **US**
    - A country with a different population composition
    - Comparatively, the US is mentioned to show a different age composition of the population, indicating Japan's unique demographic situation.
- **China**
    - Another country with a different population composition
    - Compared to Japan, China is mentioned to highlight global trends in population decline and the difference in approaches to addressing such issues.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-05**
    - The date when the article was updated and published.

## Americans still don’t know how and when to wash their hands

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/05/health/handwashing-habits-survey-wellness)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 12:01:00-20:01_

### Summary

A recent survey conducted by the National Foundation for Infectious Diseases has found that nearly half of the respondents forget or choose not to wash their hands at key times, such as after visiting grocery stores, restaurants, coffee shops, and health care settings. Despite the lessons learned during the pandemic, 33% of participants say they now wash their hands more frequently than they did during the crisis. The survey highlighted that only 30% of adults wash their hands after sneezing or coughing, which is concerning due to the potential spread of respiratory diseases. The survey also found that older adults and men are the least likely to wash their hands at important times. Dr. Robert Hopkins from the National Foundation for Infectious Diseases emphasized the importance of hand hygiene in reducing the spread of infectious diseases, stating that it is a 'nonspecific way that we can reduce risk for exposure to infectious diseases, along with dirt, grime [and] all of the other things we don’t like to see on our hands.'

### Key Takeaways
  - Some Americans still do not follow the recommended practice of handwashing, even after the pandemic.
  - Only 30% of respondents reported washing their hands after sneezing or coughing, which is concerning.
  - Public health messaging is more prevalent during colder seasons, but proper hand hygiene is essential year-round.
  - Men are more likely to forget or choose not to wash their hands, while older adults are the most diligent in their handwashing habits.

### Named Entities
- **Kristen Rogers**
    - The reporter who published the article.
    - Kristen Rogers is the author of the article, and her work is at the center of the information presented.
- **NORC**
    - The research firm that conducted the survey.
    - NORC is the entity that conducted the survey and provided data for the article, making them a key source of information.
- **National Foundation for Infectious Diseases**
    - The organization behind the 'Hands in for Handwashing Campaign'.
    - The organization is involved in raising awareness about the importance of handwashing, which is the core of this article.
- **World Hand Hygiene Day**
    - A specific day dedicated to raising awareness about hand hygiene.
    - The survey was released on this specific day, emphasizing the urgency and focus on hand hygiene.
- **Robert Hopkins**
    - The medical director of the National Foundation for Infectious Diseases.
    - He is a key expert quoted in the article, providing insights into the importance of proper hand hygiene.
- **Dr. Georges Benjamin**
    - Executive Director of the American Public Health Association.
    - He offers an expert opinion on the differences in handwashing habits among different age groups and genders, providing context to the article's findings.

    - 'The date when the survey and article was released, highlighting the current awareness and concern about hand hygiene.

## Deported from Florida to Cuba, this mom saw her 17-month-old US daughter – and her American dream – ripped away

This comes after the Trump administration was known for being more focused on dismantling diversity and equity initiatives. Assistant Attorney General Harmeet Dhillon stated that the DOJ lawyers would investigate and take action wherever necessary to identify government practices that may run against civil rights norms. The investigation, based on the policy change directing prosecutors to consider racial identity, will also review all county attorney’s office policies and practices related to illegal race consideration in prosecutorial decision-making. The Hennepin County Attorney's Office, which adopted this policy, remains confident in its compliance with the law and is cooperating with the investigation, pending receipt of the DOJ's letter.

### Key Takeaways

This incident comes amid a period where both countries are seeking to improve their diplomatic relations while navigating through the US tariff war. The extension of the deadline was seen as a move to protect TikTok from the potential ban and to maintain a favorable position for the app during the 2024 presidential election. ## Operation to recover sunken Bayesian superyacht begins off coast of Italy

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/04/europe/bayesian-superyacht-recovery-operation-intl-hnk)
- _Published: 2025-05-04 18:42:00-20:42_

### Summary

Marine salvage experts have commenced operations to recover the sunken British-flagged superyacht 'Bayesian', which sank on August 19, 2024, off the coast of Italy. This operation involves two powerful floating cranes: 'Hebo Lift 2' and 'Hebo Lift 10'. The yacht, measuring 56 meters and 473 tons, was carrying Mike Lynch, the UK tech magnate and one of the victims, along with his daughter and five others. The superyacht's recovery will likely take between 20 and 25 days. Italian coast guard officials are supervising the operation to ensure safety and security of the personnel. Judicial authorities are also investigating the sinking, focusing on the captain and two crew members. The Italian coast guard captain, Nicola Silvestri, provided details on the process, mentioning that the yacht's 75-meter-long aluminum mast will be cut to facilitate easier retrieval. The bodies of the victims, including those of Mike Lynch and his daughter, have been recovered, and search efforts for six missing people continued until August 23. The recovery operation is expected to take around 20 to 25 days, with judicial authorities examining the wreckage for further clues.

### Key Takeaways
  - Marine salvage experts are beginning the recovery operation for the sunken superyacht 'Bayesian' off the coast of Italy's Sicilian coast.
  - The operation is expected to take from 20 to 25 days, and judicial authorities will investigate the sinking.
  - The superyacht, which sank on August 19, 2024, was 56 meters (183 feet) long and 473 tons, and its 75-meter (246 feet) aluminum mast will be cut for easier retrieval from the seabed.
  - The recovery involves two floating cranes: 'Hebo Lift 2' and 'Hebo Lift 10'.
  - Judicial authorities, including prosecutors, are investigating the sinking, focusing on the captain and two crew members.
  - The operation is being supervised by the Italian coast guard to ensure personnel safety and security.
  - The initial rescue of 15 people and recovery of one body occurred soon after the sinking.
  - Search efforts continued for six missing persons, and their bodies were found after complex search efforts lasting until August 23.

### Named Entities
- **Bayesian**
    - British-flagged superyacht that sank on August 19, 2024.
    - It is the central focus of the recovery operation and the incident that occurred on the superyacht.
- **Mike Lynch**
    - The UK tech magnate who was on the superyacht 'Bayesian', and he was one of the victims of the sinking.
    - Lynch's death is mentioned as one of the victims, highlighting the tragic nature of the incident.
- **Hebo Lift 2**
    - One of the floating cranes used to recover the superyacht 'Bayesian'.
    - It is one of the tools used in the recovery operation.
- **Hebo Lift 10**
    - Another floating crane used in the recovery operation of the superyacht 'Bayesian'.
    - It is the most powerful maritime crane in Europe and is also involved in the recovery process.
- **Nicola Silvestri**
    - Capt. Nicola Silvestri, the Italian coast guard captain supervising the operations.
    - He is the one providing information about the recovery operations.
- **Morgan Stanley International**
    - The company that Jonathan Bloomer, the Morgan Stanley Chairman, was associated with.
    - It is mentioned as the affiliation of one of the victims on the superyacht 'Bayesian'.
- **Termini Imerese**
    - A port in Sicily where 'Hebo Lift 10' docked.
    - It is where one of the floating cranes docked to begin the recovery operations.

    - The country where the sunken superyacht is located.
    - It provides the geographical context for the recovery operations.

## Trump restricts funding for 'gain-of-function' research — calling it dangerous

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5267612)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 19:49:00-04:00_

### Summary

President Trump issued an executive order on May 5, 2025, restricting federal funding for 'gain-of-function' or 'dual-use' research in the United States. This controversial area of scientific study involves experimenting with viruses and pathogens, which could potentially lead to the creation of more dangerous pathogens that could cause pandemics. The executive order aims to provide powerful tools to enforce the ban on federal funding for gain-of-function research abroad and strengthens other oversight mechanisms related to this issue. Despite concerns about the broadness of the funding restriction, which could stifle safe research, many scientists argue that better oversight is needed to prevent and respond to future pandemics. The order blocks any U.S. funding of gain-of-function research in countries of concern, such as China and Iran, and prohibits U.S. dollars from contributing to foreign research likely to cause another pandemic. Supporters of the executive order, including Health and Human Services Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. and National Institutes of Health Director Jay Bhattacharya, believe it increases the safety and security of biological research without impeding U.S. innovation.

### Key Takeaways
  - President Trump issued an executive order on May 5, 2025, restricting federal funding for research that involves 'gain-of-function' or 'dual-use' research.
  - The research, which involves experimenting with viruses and pathogens, has the potential to create more dangerous pathogens that could lead to pandemics.
  - Many scientists believe the order is too broad and could stifle safe research, potentially hindering efforts to prevent or respond to future pandemics.
  - The executive order would block any U.S. funding of gain-of-function research in 'countries of concern,' such as China and Iran, and prohibit U.S. dollars from contributing to foreign research likely to cause another pandemic.

### Named Entities
- **President Trump**
    - 'The current U.S. President who issued an executive order to restrict funding for gain-of-function research.'
    - President Trump's executive order is the central event of the article, as it directly affects the research funding and safety regulations.
- **Will Scharf**
    - 'White House Secretary' who discussed the executive order's purpose.
    - 'Will Scharf's statement provides insight into the rationale behind the executive order, explaining how it strengthens oversight and enhances safety mechanisms related to this controversial research field.
- **Kristin Matthews**
    - 'Fellow in science and technology policy at Rice University's Baker Institute for Public Policy' who expressed concerns about the broadness of the funding restriction.
    - 'Kristin Matthews' perspective highlights the potential negative impact of the executive order on scientific research, as it could stifle necessary research and development.
- **Richard Ebright**
    - 'Microbiologist at Rutgers University' who supports the 'lab-leak' theory explaining the origin of the pandemic.
    - 'Richard Ebright's position demonstrates the divided opinion within the scientific community regarding the risk of gain-of-function research, reflecting the complex issue at hand.
- **Robert F. Kennedy Jr.**
    - 'Health and Human Services Secretary' who praised President Trump's decision.
    - 'Robert F. Kennedy Jr.''s statement emphasizes the administration's perspective on the necessity of the executive order in ensuring public health and safety.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-05**
    - 'This is the date when President Trump issued an executive order restricting federal funding for 'gain-of-function' research.' 

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _Now_ to _2025-05-05_**
    - 'The time frame when the executive order restricting funding for 'gain-of-function' research was issued, indicating a significant shift in U.S. government policy towards this controversial area of scientific research.

## A Maryland town backed Trump's cost-cutting pledge. Now it's a target

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5351764)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 12:01:00-20:01_

### Summary

In the small Maryland town of Emmitsburg, a stronghold for President Trump, the cancellation of National Fire Academy classes has shocked residents and sparked criticism. The academy trains firefighters and has significant economic importance for the town. Mayor Frank Davis and fire department chief Denis Onieal have expressed concern over the rapid and seemingly unnecessary cuts, viewing them as a betrayal of Trump's promise to reduce waste and spending. Local residents, including firefighters and their families, have suffered as a result of the cancellation, causing a drop in business at Ott House, a pub frequented by first responders. Senator Chris Van Hollen and other lawmakers have called for an explanation, arguing that the cuts are shortsighted and dangerous. Despite the controversy, some residents, including Susan Glass and John Beck, still support Trump's policies but believe the administration should take a more measured approach.

### Key Takeaways
  - Emmitsburg, a small Maryland town that voted heavily for President Trump, is experiencing economic distress due to the cancellation of National Fire Academy classes, which are critical for training firefighters and have a significant impact on the local economy.
  - The Trump administration canceled these classes without a clear explanation, which has surprised residents and sparked criticism for the potential impact on emergency response capabilities.
  - Many residents, including the mayor and fire department chief, have expressed frustration with the administration's decision, viewing it as a cut that is not aligned with the promised goals of reducing waste and cutting spending.
  - The cancellation has led to a significant drop in visitors to the local pub frequented by firefighters, raising concerns about the future of local businesses and employment.
  - Despite these challenges, many residents, including those who voted for Trump, believe that the administration is moving too quickly and not considering the long-term impacts of such actions.

### Named Entities
- **Frank Davis**
    - The mayor of Emmitsburg who voted for Trump and was shocked by the cancellation of National Fire Academy classes.
    - Frank Davis' perspective is pivotal to understanding the local reaction to the cancellation of the National Fire Academy classes and the implications for the community's economy and emergency response capabilities.
- **Denis Onieal**
    - A former superintendent of the National Fire Academy who trained 8-10,000 firefighters annually.
    - Onieal's expertise and experience with the National Fire Academy are crucial in explaining the critical role of the training programs in preparing first responders for various emergencies.
- **John Beck**
    - The fire chief of a nearby Pennsylvania department who applied for a leadership course at the academy.
    - John Beck's personal experience and support for the fire academy illustrate the direct impact of its cancellation on the local community and the first responders it prepares.
- **Susan Glass**
    - The co-owner of a local pub frequented by firefighters, Ott House.
    - Glass's perspective as a local resident and business owner highlights the broader economic impact of the cancellation and the community's concerns about the future of their industry.
- **Chris Van Hollen**
    - U.S. Senator from Maryland, a Democrat who has criticized the cancellation of the National Fire Academy classes.
    - Van Hollen's statements provide a political perspective on the matter and his advocacy for the continuation of the training programs.
- **Donald Trump**

## Trump's plan for movie tariffs leads to global confusion

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5387421)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 16:48:00-20:48_

### Summary

President Donald Trump announced a 100% tariff on movies produced outside the U.S. on his social media platform Truth Social, causing confusion and questions within the film and TV industry. Many American films and TV shows are produced or filmed around the world, and countries like Canada, the U.K., and Australia offer generous tax incentives. Trump gave no details on how the tariffs would work or who would pay them. A&E Studios, a production company in Hollywood, has expressed concerns about the potential impact. The film industry and unions have reacted with mixed sentiments, with some expressing support for increased incentives and others opposing the tariff plan. The reaction has been particularly strong in the U.K. and Australia, where the tariffs would significantly impact their film and TV production industries. Governor Gavin Newsom of California has been working to increase the tax incentives offered to productions in the state, in response to Trump's announcement.

### Key Takeaways
  - President Donald Trump announced a 100% tariff on movies produced outside the U.S., which has led to confusion within the film and TV industry.
  - Many American films and TV shows are produced or filmed outside the U.S., and the cost of tax incentives offered by other countries is a significant factor in their production choices.
  - There is no clear information on how the proposed tariff plan would be implemented or who would be responsible for paying the tariff, leaving the film industry with many questions.
  - The reaction to the tariff plan has been mixed, with Hollywood major film and TV studios and unions expressing concern, while other countries have stated their opposition to the tariffs.

## States sue Trump administration for blocking the development of wind energy

- [source](https://text.npr.org/g-s1-64393)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 17:45:00-20:45_

### Summary

A coalition of 17 states and Washington, D.C. filed a lawsuit against President Trump's executive order, signed during his first day in office, to stop the development of wind energy projects both onshore and offshore. The states argue that Trump has no authority to unilaterally shut down the permitting process and that the move is jeopardizing their economic vitality and climate goals. The lawsuit was filed in federal court in Massachusetts. The Trump administration, in contrast, claims that the Biden administration's policies are the problem, as Biden has supported wind energy, while Trump's policies have been more aggressive against wind energy development, aiming to boost fossil fuels and reduce domestic energy production. The lawsuit aims to declare the executive order unlawful and stop federal agencies from implementing it, arguing that it contradicts the Biden administration's goals and contradicts Trump's own declaration of a 'national energy emergency' to expand domestic energy production.

### Key Takeaways
  - A coalition of 17 states and Washington, D.C. filed a lawsuit against President Trump's executive order to stop the development of wind energy, challenging the order as unlawful and seeking to halt its implementation.

    - These entities are the main entities that are challenging the executive order and seeking a halt to its implementation.

    - The U.S. President who signed the executive order.
    - He is the main actor in the executive order and is the target of the lawsuit.

    - The Democrats representing the states who filed the lawsuit.
    - They are opposing the Trump administration's executive order and argue for its unlawful nature.

    - The lead attorney general in the coalition who filed the lawsuit.
    - She represents the states in the lawsuit and is leading the coalition against the Trump administration's order.
- **Massachusetts**
    - The state where the lawsuit was filed.
    - The lawsuit was filed in federal court in Massachusetts, highlighting the state's interest and involvement in the case.
- **U.S. Supreme Court**
    - The judicial body that denied hearing a case brought by fishermen's organizations.
    - It played a role in the legal landscape by deciding not to hear a specific case related to offshore wind development.

    - They are the primary actors in the executive order and are being challenged in the lawsuit.

    - A Norwegian energy company involved in the wind energy project.

    - They are the contrast against Trump's administration, supporting wind energy and challenging Trump's executive order.

## Trump administration asks court to toss suit restricting access to abortion drug

### Summary

The Trump administration filed a request to dismiss a lawsuit filed by three Republican-led states seeking to restrict access to the abortion medication mifepristone via telehealth. The Department of Justice argued the states lack legal standing to sue, citing the time limit to file such a claim. The case, originally filed after the Supreme Court's decision to preserve access to mifepristone, is being considered by U.S. District Judge Matthew Kacsmaryk in Texas. Kacsmaryk, a Trump nominee, previously ruled in favor of halting approval for the drug in a lawsuit filed by anti-abortion groups. The states argue that the FDA should prohibit telehealth prescriptions, require in-office visits, and restrict the use of mifepristone in pregnancy. The Trump administration's stance aligns with his past statements opposing restrictions on abortion medication, such as his decision to appoint justices to the Supreme Court who had the majority in overturning Roe v. Wade in 2022.

### Key Takeaways

    - A news publication.
    - The source of a December 2025 quote from the President about his stance on abortion medication.

## Pulitzer Prizes Announced: 'James' by Percival Everett Wins Fiction Prize

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5381150)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 16:48:00.000-04:00_

### Summary

The 2025 Pulitzer Prize winners were announced on May 5th, including Percival Everett for Fiction with his novel 'James' and Ann Telnaes for Illustrated Reporting and Commentary. The prize recognizes excellence in journalism, books, drama, and music, and this year's winners were chosen amid the ongoing challenges faced by the media industry. The novel 'James' by Percival Everett reimagines Mark Twain's 'Huckleberry Finn' from the perspective of Jim, Huck's enslaved companion, sparking critical attention. Ann Telnaes' cartoon mocking media and tech leaders' deference to President Donald Trump was rejected and later won the award, highlighting the tension between artistic expression and political influence. Other notable winners include the staff of The Washington Post for breaking news reporting and The New Yorker for illustrated reporting and commentary, emphasizing the diverse range of journalistic and literary achievements recognized by the Pulitzer Prize.

### Key Takeaways
  - James, by Percival Everett, won the 2025 Pulitzer Prize for Fiction for a reimagining of Huckleberry Finn from the perspective of Jim, Huck's enslaved companion.
  - Ann Telnaes won the Pulitzer Prize for Illustrated Reporting and Commentary for her work at The Washington Post, where she drew cartoons that were later rejected for featuring a political cartoon mocking media and tech leaders' deference to President Donald Trump.
  - The Pulitzer Prizes recognize excellence in journalism, books, drama, and music, with over 2,500 entries annually, reviewed by more than 80 editors, publishers, writers, and educators.
  - The prizes acknowledge journalists and writers who demonstrate courage, impactful storytelling, and a commitment to standing up for their values, even in the face of threats, attacks, and financial pressures.

## In 'Sinners,' the blues is a portal between this world and the next

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5381034)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 11:26:00-04:00_

### Summary

The film 'Sinners' is a reimagining of the Southern Gothic vampire story set in 1932 Mississippi that revolves around the blues, a force that can bring healing to communities but also attract evil. Writer and director Ryan Coogler understands this duality, showing how the blues can be both a source of sin and salvation. The film also explores the historical context of the blues, acknowledging its role as a precursor to many modern forms of music, including hip-hop. The article discusses how the blues, as depicted in the film, is a nexus point along the continuum of Black music, birthing so many modern forms. It highlights the tension between secularism and religious elements within the blues genre, exemplified by characters in the film who navigate the blues as a means to deal with the harsh realities of their lives, both past and present.

### Key Takeaways
  - The film 'Sinners' is a blues movie that understands the inherently duality of the blues, as a force bred of blasphemy, the godless music of boozing and fornication and infidelity, yet also a force for healing and salvation in the Mississippi Delta community's evaluations of righteousness and iniquity.

## Fast-moving Eta Aquarid meteor shower to light up the predawn sky

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5387434)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 16:26:00.000Z_

### Summary

On May 6, the annual Eta Aquarid meteor shower is expected to peak with around 50 meteors per hour, providing a spectacular sky show. The shower originates from the debris of Halley's Comet and will be visible from areas with minimal light pollution. If viewed from the Northern Hemisphere, about 10 to 20 meteors per hour are expected, while those in the Southern Hemisphere can potentially see up to 50 meteors per hour. The best time to watch is between 3 a.m. and dawn on May 6, when the moon sets and the sky is darker. To get the best viewing experience, it is recommended to find an open, dark area, lie on a comfortable surface facing east, and allow your eyes to adjust to the darkness.

### Key Takeaways
  - The annual Eta Aquarid meteor shower is expected to peak early Tuesday morning with around 50 meteors per hour, providing a spectacle for sky watchers.

### Named Entities
- **Eta Aquarid meteor shower**
    - The meteor shower that will be visible on May 6.
    - This is the main topic of the article and the reason for the public to be notified about the event.
- **NASA**
    - The space agency that provides meteor shower information.
    - NASA's information about the meteor shower is key to the public knowing when and how to view the event.
- **Halley's Comet**
    - The origin of the Eta Aquarid meteor shower.
    - The mention of Halley's Comet helps readers understand the history and origin of the meteor shower.
- **Jaclyn Diaz**
    - The author of the news article.
    - She is the source of the information about the Eta Aquarid meteor shower.
- **U.S. space agency**
    - NASA, which provides meteor shower information.
    - NASA is the authority providing meteor shower information in the article.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-06**

## Trump says he will reopen Alcatraz for the 'most ruthless and violent' prisoners

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5387239)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 16:03:00-20:03_

### Summary

President Donald Trump has announced plans to rebuild and reopen Alcatraz, a notorious maximum security prison that closed over 60 years ago, to house the 'most ruthless and violent' offenders. Historically, Alcatraz served as a prison for dangerous criminals and was seen as a symbol of the government's commitment to addressing crime and public safety. However, the proposal to reopen the prison is met with skepticism due to its high costs and logistical challenges, including water and sewage issues. The National Park Service and the Federal Bureau of Prisons have been referred for comment on the feasibility of the plan. As a result, the decision to reopen Alcatraz would require addressing both historical and modern-day challenges associated with maintaining a prison on an island.

## Minor infractions lead to big problems for international students

- [source](https://text.npr.org/g-s1-64338)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 16:08:00-20:00_

### Summary

Thousands of international students were told they had lost permission to study and work in the U.S. and would likely have to leave, including this man, who recently got his master's degree at the University of South Florida. His troubles apparently started with a minor traffic violation a few years ago, when he was charged with failing to yield to a police officer. In court, the man explained he had been waiting for a safe place to pull off the highway. But that single dismissed charge has now upended his life. His student visa registration allowed him to continue his training and work. That was abruptly terminated last month, forcing him to resign from his first job at the Florida Department of Revenue. The man, who has joined a lawsuit with other international students, believes his troubles began with a minor traffic violation a few years ago and was forced to resign from his job. Starting in March, officials at ICE ran the names of more than 1 million international students through the National Crime Information Center, a federal database that tracks crime-related information. ICE came up with about 6,400 likely hits and then used that data to terminate thousands of SEVIS records. The problem, immigration lawyers say, is that many of those hits were for minor brushes with the law, including traffic offenses, or cases where charges were later dropped or dismissed by police and courts. The Trump administration confirmed in court that it terminated immigration records for thousands of international students because of past encounters with law enforcement, causing significant confusion and legal issues for these students.

### Key Takeaways
  - International students were affected by the Trump administration's efforts to terminate their immigration records because of past minor law enforcement encounters, causing significant disruptions to their lives and studies.

## Trump cuts baby 'Safe to Sleep' team. Here's what parents should know

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5383871)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 05:00:00-04:00_

### Summary

The Trump administration has shut down the office responsible for leading the Safe to Sleep campaign, a public awareness effort launched in 1994 to reduce infant mortality rates from sleep-related causes. This shutdown, occurring on April 1, 2025, comes at a time when sleep-related infant deaths have risen by nearly 12% since 2020. The campaign, originally called Back to Sleep, has previously seen significant success, reducing deaths from Sudden Infant Death Syndrome (SIDS) by 50%. Since its termination, no final decision has been made regarding the future of the Safe to Sleep campaign. However, materials are still available online. The discontinuation of the campaign has raised concerns among researchers and organizations like First Candle, which hopes to continue educating parents on safe sleep recommendations but lacks the funding to replace the resources provided by the NIH. This situation has led to an increase in the number of parents not receiving the necessary information on safe sleep practices, potentially leading to increased risk of infant deaths.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Trump administration has shut down the office responsible for leading the Safe to Sleep campaign, which was responsible for providing information on safe infant sleep and reducing sleep-related infant deaths.

### Named Entities
- **Safe to Sleep**

    - The underlying issue the campaign aimed to address, as its discontinuation can have a significant impact on infant mortality rates.

## Black Dandyism takes the spotlight at the 2025 Met Gala

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5372642)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 13:46:00-20:00_

### Summary

Ruth E. Carter, the first Black woman to win an Oscar for costume design, has curated this year's Costume Institute Spring Exhibit at the Metropolitan Museum of Art, titled 'Superfine: Tailoring for Black Style,' which honors Black dandyism. This theme, reflecting on the fashion narrative and history of the Black dandy, highlights the aesthetic of Black dandyism as a form of performance, identity, and individuality. Carter asserts that Black dandyism is not just an act of defiance, but also a celebration of self-esteem and self-definition. The exhibition explores how Black communities have used fashion as a vehicle to express themselves, from the zoot suit riots of the 1940s to the contemporary fashion scene. The Met Gala theme underscores the importance of celebrating centuries of Black fashion history, allowing costume design, storytelling, and fashion to converge. The event is expected to showcase the full dimensionality of Black communities, marking a significant moment in the fashion world's recognition and celebration of Black heritage and style.

## 'Supermarket displays of oranges will never look the same after reading 'Foreign Fruit''

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5377392)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 14:54:00.000Z_

### Summary

In her memoir 'Foreign Fruit: A Personal History of the Orange,' author Katie Goh uses the citrus fruit as a metaphor to explore her own complex identity and connections to various cultures and histories. Goh, a queer person of Chinese, Malaysian, and Irish heritage, weaves personal and historical narratives, tracing the global journey of the orange from its origin in China to its presence in various European empires. Her memoir also reflects on her personal travels and family history, mirroring her own family tree and experiences in relation to British colonization. The author's journey-oriented structure, however, can be limiting as it restricts sustained reflection, and her final chapter is interrupted by celebratory fireworks, preventing a deeper meditation on the shooting incident in California. The book offers a unique lens through which readers can view the fruit, challenging their understanding of it.

### Key Takeaways
  - Katie Goh's memoir 'Foreign Fruit: A Personal History of the Orange' explores the history and cultural significance of the orange through a hybrid memoir that weaves personal and historical narratives.
  - The orange, a fruit with inherent genetic diversity, serves as a metaphor for hybridity, helping Goh to explore her own complex identity and connections.
  - Goh's memoir traces the global journey of the orange, from its origin in China to its presence in various European empires, and parallels this journey with her own family history and personal experiences.
  - The author, Goh, combines personal and historical narratives to reveal the complexities of identity and cultural history.
  - However, the memoir's journey-oriented structure can be limiting, as it restricts sustained reflection, and its final chapter is interrupted by celebratory fireworks, preventing a deeper meditation on the shooting incident in California.
