## Skype, the pioneering online video calling service, will shut down on 2025-05-05.

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5387436)
- _Published: 2025-05-05 15:39:00-04:00_

### Summary

Skype, the pioneering online video calling service that has been around for over two decades, will shut down entirely on 2025-05-05. Microsoft, which owns Skype, announced in February that the service would be available until May 5 and urged users to switch to the free version of Microsoft Teams, its communication platform with video call capabilities. Microsoft claims Skype users can automatically migrate all of their chats and contacts to Teams. However, the user base has been dwindling in recent years due to competition from other video calling and messaging alternatives such as Zoom, WhatsApp, and Slack. The service has been available since 2003, founded by Niklas Zennström and Janus Friis, who began with offering phone calls over the internet. By 2005, eBay had acquired Skype for $2.6 billion, which later was sold to a group of investors in 2009, who in turn sold Skype to Microsoft. Despite its decline, Microsoft suggests that users can migrate their accounts to Teams, making the transition seamless.

### Key Takeaways
  - Skype, the pioneer of online video calling, will shut down completely on 2025-05-05.
  - Skype users can migrate all chats and contacts to Microsoft's Teams platform.

### Named Entities
- **Skype**
    - The video calling service that is shutting down.
    - It is the central focus of the article detailing its impending shutdown.
- **Niklas Zennström**
    - One of the founders of Skype.
    - He is credited with founding Skype in 2003.
- **Janus Friis**
    - The co-founder of Skype.
    - He is credited with founding Skype in 2003.
- **Microsoft**
    - The company that owns and plans to shut down Skype.
    - It is the entity responsible for the announcement and future migration of users to its platform.
- **Jeff Teper**
    - Microsoft's president of collaborative apps and platforms.
    - He made a statement in a blog post about Skype's future, reflecting on its history and service to users.
- **Microsoft Teams**
    - Microsoft's communication platform with video calling capabilities.
    - It is the platform Microsoft has suggested users switch to as an alternative for their video calling needs.
- **Niklas Zennström**
    - One of the founders of Skype.
    - He is a key figure in the history of Skype's founding and growth.
- **Janus Friis**
    - The co-founder of Skype.
    - He is a key figure in the history of Skype's founding and growth.
- **2025-05-05**
    - The date Skype will shut down.
    - It marks the end of Skype's service.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-05**
    - The key event marked by the shutdown announcement of Skype.

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _2020_ to _2025-05-05_**
    - The timeframe during which Skype's user base has been decreasing.

## Does a president need to uphold the Constitution? Trump says 'I don't know'

- [source](https://text.npr.org/g-s1-64239)
- _Published: 2025-05-04 10:58:00-20:58_

### Summary

President Trump, when asked about his need to uphold the Constitution during an interview with 'Meet the Press with Kristen Welker,' stated, 'I don't know,' but added that his lawyers would follow Supreme Court rulings. This came in the context of his recent statements about deporting millions of undocumented immigrants and his plans to lower interest rates quickly. The interview also touched upon Trump's views on the Federal Reserve and the potential for a recession. He ruled out a third term and defended his trade policies, including tariffs, which he claimed would make the U.S. rich. Trump also predicted a favorable economic future for the country despite economic reports indicating a recession. When questioned about criticisms of his leadership, Trump confirmed he believes his critics have the right to speak against him without fear of retribution.

### Key Takeaways
  - President Trump stated he does not believe he needs to uphold the Constitution.
  - The President emphasized his lawyers would follow Supreme Court rulings on constitutional matters.
  - Trump expressed his intention to deport millions of undocumented immigrants.
  - Trump ruled out running for a third term.
  - The President criticized Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell's decision to not lower interest rates quickly.
  - Trump defended his tariffs on global trade and suggested they might become permanent.
  - Trump predicted a favorable economic future for the country through his policies, despite the economic reports indicating a recession in the first quarter.
